plt.show()




# kstest
stats.kstest(y , 'norm')
Output: 
KstestResult(statistic=0.5000241388491746, pvalue=0.0)


# from above we clearly see than Dn,m is greater the pvalue
# so we reject H0 and accept H1
# so y is not a gaussian distribution




Hypothesis testing: another example:
                                                                              * Below example of Difference of means:
                                                                              * Task: 
                                                                              * Given heights of two cities A and B, determine if the population means of heights in these two cities is the same or not.
                                                                              * Let the population mean of both cities are μ1 and μ2.
                                                                              * Experiment: 
                                                                              * We cannot collect the whole population data so we will take a sample.
                                                                              * Collect a height of 50 random people from both the cities.
                                                                              * Compute sample means from both cities μAand μB.
                                                                              * Let μA = 162 cm and μB = 167 cm
                                                                              * These are sample means as population data collection is infeasible.
                                                                              * Test statistic:
                                                                              * Let x = μB –  μA
                                                                              * Difference of sample mean heights of A and B with sample sizes 50.
                                                                              * Observation(which is ground truth): 
                                                                              * x = μB –  μA = 167 – 62 = 5 cm
                                                                              * Null hypothesis:
                                                                              * μB –  μA = 0
                                                                              * There is no difference in population means of the two cities.
                                                                              * Alternative hypothesis:
                                                                              * μB –  μA != 0
                                                                              * There is a difference in means of height values of two cities.
                                                                              * Compute :
                                                                              *  P(x = 5 cm | H0 )
                                                                              * probability of observing a difference of 5 cm in the sample mean of sample size 50 between two cities A and B if there is no population difference in mean heights.
                                                                              * Case 1:
                                                                              * P(x = 5 cm | H0 ) = 0.2 = 20%
                                                                              * There is a 20% chance of observing 5% difference in sample mean heights of A and B with 50 sample sizes if there is no population mean difference in heights.
                                                                              * As 20% is significant then the null hypothesis must be true.
                                                                              * We accept the null hypothesis.
                                                                              * Case 2:
                                                                              * P(x = 5 cm | H0 ) = 0.03 = 3%
                                                                              * There is a 3% chance of observing 5% difference in sample mean heights of C1 and C2 with 50 sample sizes if there is no population mean difference in heights.
                                                                              * As 3% is insignificant then the null hypothesis must be False.
                                                                              * We reject the null hypothesis and accept the alternative hypothesis.


                                                                              * Note: for not confusing  in hypothesis testing go with this flow:
                                                                              * Task → Experiment → Test statistic → Observation →  Null hypothesis → Compute




Re-sampling and Permutation test(another example):
                                                                              * Test statistic:
                                                                              * x = μB –  μA 
                                                                              * with sample size of 50
                                                                              * Observation:
                                                                              * μB –  μA = 167 – 62 = 5 cm
                                                                              * Null hypothesis:
                                                                              * x = μB –  μA = 0
                                                                              * no difference in population means
                                                                              * Step 1:
                                                                              * List of A and B heights.
                                                                              * S = A U B = set of 100 heights
                                                                              * Step 2:
                                                                              * From set S, randomly select 50 heights for SA and 50 heights for SB (This is called resampling).
                                                                              * And compute means of these SA and SB heights.
                                                                              * Let means of SA and SB are μSA and μSB. 
                                                                              * We have re-sampled the data set, with this we are making an assumption that there is no difference in μB and  μA which is the null hypothesis.
                                                                              * Compute: μSB - μSA
                                                                              * Let μSB - μSA = δ1
                                                                              * Step 3:
                                                                              * Repeat Step 2 for k times, let k = 1000
                                                                              * Result:
                                                                              * we will have 1000 ( μSB - μSA) { δ1, δ2, .... , δ1000 }
                                                                              *  { δ1, δ2, .... , δ1000 } these are simulated differences.
                                                                              * Sort these, these are simulated differences under null hypothesis.
                                                                              * simulated differences under null hypothesis:
                                                                              * “It means that if we randomly select 50 - 50 value from SA and SB and compute mean then if class A and B has no difference in their heights then there is insignificante difference in means μSB - μSA so the resampling is a way for us to simulate the null hypothesis.”
                                                                              * we will have 1000 (μSB - μSA) (sorted) and we have μB –  μA = 5 cm (observed).
                                                                              * Now we have to compute P(x 5 | H0 ).
                                                                              * Compute the percentage of simulated differences of means that are greater than observed test statistics.
                                                                              *  This is the p-value which can be checked for significance at α level.
                                                                                 * Note: 
                                                                                 * Simulated differences are computed using Null Hypothesis.
                                                                                 * P( x = 5 | H0 ):
                                                                                 *  The difference exactly equals 5 cm in simulated difference of mean  = p-value.
                                                                                 * if p-value > 5% accept null hypothesis else reject null hypothesis.
                                                                                 * Observed differences can never be incorrect as it is ground truth generated from the data.
                                                                                 * Acceptance or rejection happens with null hypothesis.




How to use hypothesis testing?
                                                                                 * Determining two random variables that follow the same distribution or not.
                                                                                 * Drug testing: 
                                                                                 * Let there are two durg D1 and D2 from company C1 and C2.
                                                                                 * D1 durg from company C1 is more famous and available in the market and it reduces fever in 4 hour.
                                                                                 * D2 durg from company C2 is new in the market and claims to reduce fever significantly faster than durg D1.
                                                                                 * Task :
                                                                                 * To determine if the claim is true or not.
                                                                                 * Experiment:
                                                                                 * Collect 100 patients randomly split into two groups of 50 people each.
                                                                                 * Administer old drug to group A and new drug to group B.
                                                                                 * record time taken for all the 100 people to recover.
                                                                                 * Let the mean time for old drug people be 4 hours and for new drug people be 2 hours.
                                                                                 * Mean tells that the new drug is performing well.
                                                                                 * Note that the sample size is 50 ,if we have a sample greater than 50 then the mean may be changed so hypothesis is applied.
                                                                                 * H0:
                                                                                 * Old drug and the new drug take the same amount of time to recover.
                                                                                 * Test statistic:
                                                                                 * Let X = μold – μnew
                                                                                 * Difference in mean of time taken between old and new drug.
                                                                                 * Observation:
                                                                                 * X = μold – μnew = 2 hours
                                                                                 * Compute :
                                                                                 * P(X >=  2 | H0 ) =  (let = 1%) :
                                                                                 * Probability of observing the difference in μold – μnew greater the 2 hour if there is no difference in time taken to recover in both drug.
                                                                                 * If there is no difference in old drug and new drug then the probability of observing  μold – μnew >= 2 is 1%.
                                                                                 * This implies that the null hypothesis and observation do not agree with each other, thus the null hypothesis is incorrect.
                                                                                 * P-value:
                                                                                 * agreement between null hypothesis and the test statistic.
                                                                                 * Probability value is computed using re-sampling and permutation test.
                                                                                 * Combine the datasets into 1 large set and sample randomly and compute test statistics for samples and sort the results.
                                                                                 * Find the percentage of values that are greater than the original test statistic value.
                                                                                 * Significance level is problem specific.
                                                                                 * For problems such as medical tests, the significance level is 0.1% or1%.
                                                                                 * For ecommerce 3% or 5% are generally taken.
                                                                                 * Can be used for computing average spending of a set of people.


Proportional Sampling:
                                                                                 * Let d: [d1, d2, d3, d4, d5] = [2.0, 6.0, 1.2, 5.8, 20.0]
                                                                                 * Task:
                                                                                 * pick an element from the list such that the probability of picking the element is proportional to the value.
                                                                                 * For random selection the probability of picking any value is equal to all other values, but the task requires proportional sampling:
                                                                                 * Compute sum of all the elements in the list: = 35.0
                                                                                 * Divide list with the sum(normalizing using sum), list = [0.0571, 0.171428, 0.0343, 0.1657, 0.5714]
                                                                                 * Sum of all these values are between 0 and 1
                                                                                 * Cumulate normalized sum: C_list = [0.0571, 0.228528, 0.262828, 0.428528, 1.00]
                                                                                 * Sample one value from Uniform distribution between 0 and 1.
                                                                                 * let r = 0.6
                                                                                 * Use the index from C_list where r <= value in C_list and return the original value at the index at which r is placed.
                                                                                 * In C_list the gap between values is proportional to the original values, as random number r is generated from a uniform distribution, the probability of picking any value is equal to the gap between the elements in C_list in turn proportional to the original list values.

Chapter 3: Dimensionality Reduction and visualisation
________________




What is Dimensionality Reduction?
                                                                                 * We can visualize 2D and 3D using Scatter Plots, up to 6D we can leverage Pair Plots. 
                                                                                 * For nD > 6D we should reduce the dimensionality to make it an understandable or a visualizable dataset.
                                                                                 * Techniques:
                                                                                 *  tSNE and PCA
                                                                                 * By reducing dimensionality, we transform the features into a new set of features which are less in number. The aim lies in preserving the variance which ensures least possible loss of information.


Row Vector and Column Vector
                                                                                 *   where, xi is values d is the dimension of the d-dimensional column vector,R is the real number(or space) and several data points are stacked in row wise to form a dataset.


How to represent a data set?
                                                                                    * Let represent for iris dataset:
                                                                                    *   where,
                                                                                    *    means that x is d dimension column vector.
  

                                                                                       * So,   
                                                                                       *                                                                                          *   

How to represent a dataset as a Matrix?
                                                                                          * Matrix is like a table
                                                                                          *                                                                                             * where, fd (columns) are features of a dataset.
                                                                                          * Rows are the datapoint
                                                                                          * In many research papers matrices are represented like XT where data points are columns and features are rows.
                                                                                          * Y is a column matrix/vector in which each data point in Y, corresponds to the row in X so we can say that XI corresponds to Yi




 
Data Preprocessing: Feature Normalization
                                                                                             * Data preprocessing: 
                                                                                             * Mathematical transformations on Data to make it Machine readable by improving its quality and reducing the dimensionality (sometimes).
                                                                                             * Column Normalization:
                                                                                             * We process each column one by one.
                                                                                             * For each column, which corresponds to a feature, we take all its values and normalize them by subtracting the minimum value and then dividing by the range of the feature.
                                                                                             * Let a1, a2, a3, …, an are one feature of the matrix let assume that ai are petal length of all 150 flowers.
                                                                                             * max(ai) = amax and min(ai) = amin 
                                                                                             * So from column normalization we make  a’i such that:
                                                                                             *                                                                                                * From that  the range of    
                                                                                             * The column normalization method transforms all the features to a range from 0 to 1.
                                                                                             * Column Normalization is needed to avoid different feature scales.   
                                                                                             * Some variables may take values between 1 million and 2 million, while others may only take values between 0 and 10. Without normalization, the second feature becomes insignificant to the model because larger values will have a greater impact during the prediction stage.
                                                                                             * Through column normalization, we eliminate these differing feature scales. This process squishes the n-dimensional data into a unit hypercube, ensuring all features contribute equally to the model.




Mean of a data matrix:
                                                                                                * Mean is the central value for scalers similarly mean vector is the central vector of vectors.
                                                                                                * Mean of data matrix means that all the data is form of vector example: 
                                                                                                * A = [a1, b1] and B = [a2, b2] so if we want to find the average or mean of the data or vector we sum all components and divide by the number of data. Here n = 2 (  )
                                                                                                *    { where xi is vector    and    is mean of vector}
                                                                                                * So this is also called mean of a vectors
                                                                                                   * Geometrically: 
                                                                                                   * Project all data points onto each feature axis.
                                                                                                   * The central vector of all these projections is the mean on each feature axis.
                                                                                                   * The set of the means is the mean vector of the data matrix.


Data Pre-processing: Column Standardization:


                                                                                                   * Column Standardization: 
                                                                                                   * In a data matrix, with rows as data points and columns as features a1, a2, a3, a4, …., an for each feature are transformed to a1’, a2’, a3’, ….., an’ such that:
                                                                                                   *                                                                                                      * With standardization, we will have mean =0 and std_dev = 1
                                                                                                   * It uses standard normal variates to standardise the values.
                                                                                                      * Column Standardization = Mean Centering + unit scaling
                                                                                                      * Geometrically: 
                                                                                                      * Project all data points on feature axes, we can get mean and standard deviation of the dataset. 
                                                                                                      * After applying column standardization the data points will have mean at origin (mean vector) and the data points are transformed to a unit standard deviation.
                                                                                                      *   

  



Co-variance of a Data Matrix:
                                                                                                         * X = n x d matrix, its covariance matrix is S  of size d x d (square 
matrix)
                                                                                                         * fj = column vector – jth feature
                                                                                                         * xi,j = value of ith datapoint and jth feature in X.
                                                                                                         * Si,j = ith row and jth column in covariance matrix, is a square matrix  


                                                                                                            *   





                                                                                                               *             
          
                                                                                                                  * In a covariance matrix, we have diagonal elements as variance(because j == i) values and the matrix is symmetric(Ai,j = Aj,i).
                                                                                                                  * So our covariance matrix is a square symmetric matrix.
                                                                                                                  *                                                                                                                     *   (because mean become zero when we column standardized)


                                                                                                                     * So,   
                                                                                                                     *                                                                                                                           * S(X) we get a covariance matrix if we multiply a matrix by its transpose and divide by the number of rows.

                                                                                                                        * Each data point: xi = Image (28 x28),  yi = {0, 1…., 9}
                                                                                                                        * Dimensionality reduction: from 2D to 1D using Flattening operation (28 x 28) is converted into (784 x 1) shape, by stacking all elements from each row into a column vector We can use PCA or tSNE to visualize the dataset using different technique.

Chapter 4: PCA
________________




Why learn PCA?( **article ) (statquest video )
                                                                                                                        * PCA – for dimensionality reduction - R^d to R^ d’ where d’ << d
                                                                                                                        * It is use for:
                                                                                                                        * For visualization (learning now)
                                                                                                                        * d’ < d (dimensional reduction) for model training (learning after some chapter)




Geometric intuition of PCA
  



                                                                                                                        * If we want to reduce dimensionality from 2D to 1D, we can skip feature f1 as the spread across the feature is very less than spread across the feature f2 (because more spread or variance more information) .
                                                                                                                        * Another case: Let y = x be the underlying relationship between two features and let X be column standardized, and the plot is such that there is sufficient variance on both features. Say, we rotate the axes and reach an orientation were spread on f2’ << f 1 ’ (perpendicular to f2’) then we can drop f2’.
                                                                                                                        *  So data transformation can also find maximum variance features. This will help us reduce dimensionality.
                                                                                                                        * Our objective is:
                                                                                                                        * We want to find a direction f 1 ’ such that the variance of the data points projected onto f 1 ’ is maximum and we can skip  f2’ features with minimum spread.
  





Mathematical objective function of PCA:


variance maximization formulation of PCA:
                                                                                                                        * u1 : Unit vector: in the direction where maximum variance of projection of xi exists
                                                                                                                        * || u1 ||  = 1
                                                                                                                        * xi‘ = proj xi in u1 = 
                                                                                                                        *  from this we can get any point Xi in line u1
                                                                                                                        * If xi = x_bar (mean) then  is a mean vector in line u1.
  



                                                                                                                           * Task:
                                                                                                                           * find u1 , such that the variance of projection of xi in u1 is maximum.(because we want an unit vector(direction) u1 such that the maximum point(variance) lies in that direction).
                                                                                                                           *                                                                                                                                 * where x_bar is mean
                                                                                                                              * Now if we column standardized:
                                                                                                                              * Then x_bar becomes zero.
                                                                                                                              * Then variance is:
                                                                                                                              *                                                                                                                                    * We want u1 such that the above equation(variance) is maximum.
                                                                                                                                 * This is optimization problem:
                                                                                                                                 * Objective:
                                                                                                                                 *                                                                                                                                       * Constraint: 
                                                                                                                                    *                                                                                                                                       * u1 is always a unit vector. 




Alternative formulation of PCA: 
Distance Normalization formulation of PCA:


                                                                                                                                       * Distance Normalization:
                                                                                                                                       *   

                                                                                                                                          * Task:
                                                                                                                                          * find u1 such that distances of the data points to u1 is minimum.
                                                                                                                                          * u1 is unit vector.
                                                                                                                                          * Objective: 
                                                                                                                                          * Projection of Xi in u1 :    
                                                                                                                                          *                                                                                                                                             *                                                                                                                                                * Constraint: 
                                                                                                                                             *                                                                                                                                                   * With some simple transformation in optimization we can prove that the u1 which achieves minimization(in distance minimization) is the same as the u1 which maximizes(variance maximization) . We can prove this later.


Eigenvalues and Eigenvectors:
                                                                                                                                                * Let we have a Covariance matrix S , and we know the Covariance matrix is column standardized which means each column mean is 0, and variance of each column is 1.
                                                                                                                                                * And also S is a square symmetric matrix of (d * d) dimensions( see covariance matrix for reference).
                                                                                                                                                * Solution to the optimization problems:
                                                                                                                                                * Eigenvalue of S: λ1 , λ2 , λ3 , λ4 , …. (λ1 > λ2 > λ3 > λ4 …. )
                                                                                                                                                * Eigenvectors of S: V1, V2 , V3, V4 , …
                                                                                                                                                * λ1 corresponds to V1 , λ2 corresponds to V2 and so on.
                                                                                                                                                * Def: If λ1 V1 = Sdxd V1, satisfy then λ1 and V1 are Eigenvalue and Eigenvector.
                                                                                                                                                *  λ1 is a scalar which is the Eigenvalue of S and V1 of dimensions (d * 1) is the Eigenvector corresponding to λ1.
                                                                                                                                                * If S is (d* d) dimension then there are d numbers of pairs of eigenvalues and eigenvectors.
                                                                                                                                                * Eigen vectors are perpendicular to each other. This implies that the dot product of pairs of Eigen vectors is zero. ViT Vj = 0
                                                                                                                                                * Now our u1 = V1 = Eigenvector of S (= XTX) corresponding to largest Eigenvalues (= λ1 ).( we can prove this later)
                                                                                                                                                * Steps to find:
                                                                                                                                                * X: Column Standardized
                                                                                                                                                * S = XTX * 1/n ( covariance matrix)
                                                                                                                                                * Compute the values of eigenvalue and eigenvector. λ1 , V1 = eigen(s).
                                                                                                                                                * u1 = V1 direction with maximum variance.
                                                                                                                                                * Geometric interpretations:
                                                                                                                                                *    = % of variance preserved on u1 , V1 max variance, V2 second max var, V3 third max var, …
                                                                                                                                                * Eigen Vectors provide direction of maximum variance(u1).
                                                                                                                                                * Eigen values provide a percentage of variance preserved with each Eigenvector.
  

                                                                                                                                                   * IP = information preserved
                                                                                                                                                   * In the first diagram we get all points in V1, and V2 has no spread so if we reduce it to one dimension then we lose 0% of information. (IP = 100%)
                                                                                                                                                   * In the second diagram we get ¾ points in V1 and V2 has ¼ points so if we reduced it to one dimension then we lose 25% of information.(IP = 100%)
                                                                                                                                                   * In the third diagram we get ⅗ points in V1 and V2 has ⅖ points so if we reduce it to one dimension then we lose 40% of information.(IP = 100%)
                                                                                                                                                   * In the second diagram we get ½ points in V1 and V2 has ½ points so if we reduced it to one dimension then we lose 50% of information.(IP = 100%)


PCA for Dimensionality Reduction and Visualization:
                                                                                                                                                   * If we have (d x d) dimensions matrix then we can reduce it to d’ by using PCA. where d >= d’.
                                                                                                                                                   * For X: Let us have S of 2 -dimensions( f1 and f2 ). We want to convert it to 1-dimensions then we can get V1 and V2  using the eigen(s) function.


                                                                                                                                                   * Transform xi = [f1i , f2i ] to xi ’ = [ f1iT V1 , f2iT V2  ] where xi is the value of matrix X and f1iT V1  = ith value of f1,column projected to vector V1.
                                                                                                                                                   *  we can drop xiT V2 as there is not much variance, 2D data point is transformed to 1D.


                                                                                                                                                   * If we want to preserve say k% of variance:
                                                                                                                                                   * Find d’ such that    where d is dimensionality of the input data point. For example d= 100 and it reduces to d’= 51 which can preserve 95% of information.








Limitations of PCA:
                                                                                                                                                      * Loss of information:
                                                                                                                                                      *  cases for hyper-spheres, separable data points on high dimensionality can get crowded at several locations making it inseparable at low Dimensionality.


  

                                                                                                                                                      * First diagram:
                                                                                                                                                      *  large percentage of information loss.
                                                                                                                                                      * Second diagram: 
                                                                                                                                                      * There are visible groups but when we reduce to 1-d then the v2 value will collapse and make us confused for separation so from PCA we can loss nice groups or clusters of data.
                                                                                                                                                      * Third diagram:
                                                                                                                                                      * It's a nice sine wave-like curve, if we reduce to 1-D and project all points to V1 then we can lose the nice structure which may help us to separate.




PCA code example MNIST dataset:


import pandas as pd
import numpy as np
import matplotlib.pyplot as plt


# loading MNIST dataset
d0 = pd.read_csv('mnist_train.csv')
# print first five rows of d0.
print(d0.head(5))
# save the labels into a variable l.
l = d0['label']
# Drop the label feature and store the pixel data in d.
d = d0.drop("label", axis= 1)
output:

from sklearn.preprocessing import StandardScaler

(42000, 784)

sample_data = standardized_data
​
#find the covariance matrix which is : (A^T * A) * 1/n
# matmul is for matrix multiplication
no_of_rows = standardized_data.shape[0]
covar_matrix = \
(1/no_of_rows) * (np.matmul(standardized_data.T,standardized_data))
print("The shape of covariance matrix = ",covar_matrix.shape)
output:
The shape of covariance matrix =  (784, 784)


# finding the top two eigen-values and corresponding eigen-vectors
# for projecting 784 DIMENSIONS Into 2 DIMENSIONS space.
from scipy.linalg import eigh
​
# the parameter 'eigvals' is defined (low value to heigh value)
# eigh function will return the eigenvalues in ascending order
# This code generates only the top 2 (782 and 783) eigenvalues because the index starts with 0.
e_values, e_vectors = eigh(covar_matrix, eigvals=(782, 783))
​
print("Shape of eigenvectors = ",e_vectors.shape)
​
# converting the eigen vectors into (2,d) shape for easiness of further computations
e_vectors = e_vectors.T
print("Updated shape of eigenvectors = ",e_vectors.shape)
Shape of eigenvectors =  (784, 2)
Updated shape of eigenvectors =  (2, 784)


In [7]:
# here the vectors[1] represent the eigenvector corresponding 1st principal eigenvector
# here the vectors[0] represent the eigenvector corresponding 2nd principal eigenvector
print(e_values)


array([29.11077253, 40.69550978])


# projecting the original(standardized) sample_data on the plane
#formed by two principal eigen vectors by vector-vector multiplication.
new_cordinates = np.matmul(e_vectors, sample_data.T)
print('new coordinates is :: ',e_vectors.shape,"X",sample_data.T.shape, " = ", new_cordinates.shape)
new coordinates is ::  (2, 784) X (784, 42000)  =  (2, 42000)

PCA for dimensionality reduction (not-visualization):
                                                                                                                                                      * d >= d’, d’ is the dimension which we want to reduce to. 
                                                                                                                                                      * If d' = 2 or 3, it is for visualization, but if d’= 200 or any other value , then we are doing data reduction for non-visualization tasks(or making models).
                                                                                                                                                      * Stack Eigen vectors horizontally to get Eigen matrix V. Multiply X(standardize matrix) with V to get X’ which is dimensionally reduced. 
                                                                                                                                                      * d' can be determined by checking explained variance .
                                                                                                                                                      * The task is to maximize variance:
                                                                                                                                                      * Explained variance = % of variance retained =   
                                                                                                                                                         * n is the number of eigen values which is added to get desired explained variance or the variance you want to get.
                                                                                                                                                         * Example:
                                                                                                                                                         * You want to get 90% of variance then put in the formula
                                                                                                                                                         * Then you can get the value of n
                                                                                                                                                         * Now our d’ = n (number of dimensions)
                                                                                                                                                         * Then d’of eigenvectors you want, to get 90% of variance.


PCA for dimensionality reduction (not for visualization)
In [17]:
# let we can take all 784 dimensions
pca.n_components = 784
​
# now our principal component is
pca_data = pca.fit_transform(sample_data)
print(pca_data.shape)
(42000, 784)




# pca.explained_variance_ is all the eigenvalues in descending order
for i in range(4):
   print(pca.explained_variance_[i])


40.69647874534515
29.11146565722667
26.78333709864516
20.814719425177486




# sum of eigenvalues
sum_of_eig_values = np.sum(pca.explained_variance_)
​
# compute percentage of each eigenvalue
percentage_var_explained = pca.explained_variance_ / sum_of_eig_values


for i in range(4):
   print(percentage_var_explained[i])


0.057479533589781764
0.04111691034899995
0.03782867146912825
0.02939862123816347


# cumulative sum to find how many eigenvalues needed to get our desire variance
cum_var_explained = np.cumsum(percentage_var_explained)


for i in range(4):
   print(cum_var_explained[i])


0.057479533589781764
0.09859644393878171
0.13642511540790997
0.16582373664607344




#Plot the PCA spectrum
plt.figure(1, figsize=(6, 4))
plt.clf()
plt.plot(cum_var_explained)
plt.axis('tight')
plt.grid()
plt.xlabel("n_components")
plt.ylabel("Cumulative_explained_variance")
plt.show()
  

                                                                                                                                                         * Now from the above figure we can say that for obtaining 90% of variance we can reduce 784 dimensions to 200(approx) dimensions.
                                                                                                                                                         * And 784 - 200 = 484 dimensions only contain 10 % of variance.
                                                                                                                                                         * Note: 200 dimensions is our first 200 principal dimensions which means the largest 200 eigenvalues.


________________
Chapter 5: T-SNE
________________


T-SNE (T-distributed Stochastic Neighborhood Embedding)
                                                                                                                                                         * t-sne(statquest)
                                                                                                                                                         * What is t-SNE?
                                                                                                                                                         * T-SNE is a iterative algorithm it solves problem step by step.
                                                                                                                                                         * One of the best techniques for data visualization.
                                                                                                                                                         * A popular method for exploring high-dimensional data is something called t-SNE, introduced by van der Maaten and Hinton in 2008.
                                                                                                                                                         * PCA – basic, old did not perform well on MNIST dataset visualization
                                                                                                                                                         * Some Other techniques for data visualization and reduction
                                                                                                                                                         * Multiple Dimensional Scaling, Sammon Mapping,UMAP,  Graph based techniques
                                                                                                                                                         * tSNE vs PCA:
                                                                                                                                                         * PCA preserves the global structure of the dataset (overall structure) and discards local structure.
                                                                                                                                                         * tSNE also preserves local structure of the dataset(how one point is placed compared to other points).


  







Neighborhood of a point, Embedding:
                                                                                                                                                         * For a d-dimension space:
                                                                                                                                                         * Neighborhood points of a data point are the points that are geometrically close to the data point.
                                                                                                                                                         *                                                                                                                                                            * In the above figure all green points are neighborhoods of red points and black points are not.
                                                                                                                                                         * N(xi) = {xj , such that xi & xj are geometrically closed} (N stands for neighborhood)
                                                                                                                                                            * Embedding:
                                                                                                                                                            * For every point in the original dataset(or higher dimensional dataset), a new point is created in the lower dimension corresponding to the original data point. 
                                                                                                                                                            * Embedding means projecting each and every input data point into another more convenient representation space (Picking a point in high dimensional space and placing it in a low dimensional space).


Geometric intuition of t-SNE
  

                                                                                                                                                            * Let us assume: x1, x2, x3, x4 and x5 are some data points in n-dimension space.
                                                                                                                                                            * Let x1, x2 and x3 be in a neighborhood region, x4 and x5 be another neighborhood region and both neighborhood regions are very far from each other.
                                                                                                                                                            * N(x1) = {x2, x3} and N(x4) = {x5}
                                                                                                                                                            * When we reduce the dimensionality from n-dimension to 2-dimension:
                                                                                                                                                            * We follow the objective of preserving the distance between neighborhood data points.
                                                                                                                                                            * dist(x1, x2) ~ dist(x1’, x2’)
                                                                                                                                                            * For points which are not in the neighborhood the distances are not preserved.
                                                                                                                                                            * Relation between dist(x1, x4) and dist(x1’, x4’) is ignored.
                                                                                                                                                            * Note:
                                                                                                                                                            * The mathematics behind t-sne is complicated, so we ignored it in this course but we will learn how to use it.
                                                                                                                                                            * T-sne 1 and T-sne 2 (mathematical oriented video)




Crowding Problem
                                                                                                                                                            * Non-neighbor data points can also be seen to crowd with neighborhood data points. 
                                                                                                                                                            * t-SNE preserves distances in a Neighborhood. It is impossible to preserve the neighborhood of all the data points.
                                                                                                                                                            * And when non-neighborhood points are crowded with neighborhood points that is called a crowding problem.
                                                                                                                                                            * Before t-sne there was research in SNE but to avoid crowding problems to some extent we use t-distribution(student t-distribution).
                                                                                                                                                            * T-distribution says “i will not guarantee that i preserve all the distances i will do my best(minimize error) to preserve the distances”
                                                                                                                                                            * Example:
                                                                                                                                                            *                                                                                                                                                               * Above N(a) = {b,d}, N(b) = {a, c}, N(d) = {a,c} . N(c) = {d,b}
                                                                                                                                                            * If we preserver c,d,b then we loss the structure of a:
                                                                                                                                                               * c is x distance from d and b
                                                                                                                                                               * d is x distance from a and c
                                                                                                                                                               * b is x distance from a and c
                                                                                                                                                               *                                                                                                                                                                  * If we project a,b,c,d in 1-D then point a is 3x distance from b(which is wrong distance) this is called crowding problem.
                                                                                                                                                                  * sometimes(especially in the case of hypercube) it is impossible to preserve distances in all the neighborhoods.
How to apply t-SNE and interpret its output?
                                                                                                                                                                  * Link: https://distill.pub/2016/misread-tsne/ *** very important
                                                                                                                                                                  * Processes all the data in multiple iterations and tries to separate different neighborhoods.
                                                                                                                                                                  * Parameters:
                                                                                                                                                                  * Step: Number of iterations
                                                                                                                                                                  * Perplexity: Loosely indicates the number of neighbors to whom distances are preserved.
                                                                                                                                                                  * Notes: 
                                                                                                                                                                  * Run tSNE with multiple perplexity values.
                                                                                                                                                                  * As perplexity increases from 1, the neighborhood tries to get good clusters and then tries to find the shapes which are more stable.
                                                                                                                                                                  * With further increments the clustered profile becomes a mess because more data points are considered to belong to the same neighborhood.
                                                                                                                                                                  * Always try to choose your perplexity value less than the number of data points.
                                                                                                                                                                  * Find the right type of perplexity by keeping your number of iteration large.
                                                                                                                                                                  * When the plot of t-sne doesn't change much, that's the number of steps you may choose.
                                                                                                                                                                  * Your perplexity should be 2<perplexity<n (number of data points).
                                                                                                                                                                  * Stochastic part of tSNE induces probabilistic embedding, results change every time tSNE is run on the same data points with same parameter values.
                                                                                                                                                                  * tSNE also expands dense clusters and shrinks sparse(wide) clusters, cluster sizes cannot be compared and tSNE doesn’t preserve cluster size and intercluster distances.
                                                                                                                                                                  * tSNE does not preserve distances between clusters.
                                                                                                                                                                  * Never rely on the results of tSNE, experiment with changing parameter values. You may need to plot multiple plots to visualize.
                                                                                                                                                                  * Never make sense of junk data(random data) with small perplexity value, try different values of perplexity values.
                                                                                                                                                                  * You can see some shapes, sometimes.
                                                                                                                                                                  * tSNE never exactly replicates the result.
                                                                                                                                                                  * If shapes change with every time you run on the same parameter then the parameter is wrong and if shape doesn't change much only some minor changes(like rotation) happen then that is the right parameter for you, so that's why you have to run multiple times.


  
  







t-SNE on MNIST
                                                                                                                                                                  * MNIST:
                                                                                                                                                                  * 784-dim data of images of hand written Numbers between 0 and 9.
                                                                                                                                                                  * tSNE:
                                                                                                                                                                  * grouped data points or images based on visual similarity;

Questions & Answers:
Question 1. You are given a train data set having 1000 columns and 1 million rows. The data set is based on a classification problem. Your manager has asked you to reduce the dimension of this data so that model computation time can be reduced. Your machine has memory constraints. What would you do? (You are free to make practical assumptions.)


Ans: Close all other applications, random sample dataset, reduce dimensionality (remove correlated features, Use correlation for Numerical and chi-square test for categorical, Can use PCA)




Question 2. Is rotation necessary in PCA? If yes, Why?(link)


Ans: Yes, rotation (orthogonal) is necessary because it maximizes the difference between variance captured by the component. This makes the components easier to interpret. Not to forget, that’s the motive of doing PCA where, we aim to select fewer components (than features) which can explain the maximum variance in the data set. By doing rotation, the relative location of the components doesn’t change, it only changes the actual coordinates of the points.
If we don’t rotate the components, the effect of PCA will diminish and we’ll have
to select more numbers of components to explain variance in the data set.




Question 3. You are given a data set. The data set contains many variables, some of which are highly correlated and you know about it. Your manager has asked you to run PCA. Would you remove correlated variables first? Why?(link)


Ans:        Chances are, you might be tempted to say No, but that would be incorrect. Discarding correlated variables has a substantial effect on PCA because, in the presence of correlated variables, the variance explained by a particular component gets inflated.
For example: You have 3 variables in a data set, of which 2 are correlated. If you run PCA on this data set, the first principal component would exhibit twice the variance than it would exhibit with uncorrelated variables. Also, adding correlated variables lets PCA put more importance on those variables, which is misleading.

Chapter 1: Real world problem : predict rating given product reviews on amazon
________________
DATASET OVERVIEW: AMAZON FINE FOOD REVIEWS (EDA):
                                                                                                                                                                  * Amazon largest retailers of the world


Amazon Fine Food Reviews Analysis
Data Source: https://www.kaggle.com/snap/amazon-fine-food-reviews


EDA: https://nycdatascience.com/blog/student-works/amazon-fine-foods-visualization/


The Amazon Fine Food Reviews dataset consists of reviews of fine foods from Amazon.


                                                                                                                                                                  1. Number of reviews: 568,454
                                                                                                                                                                  2. Number of users: 256,059
                                                                                                                                                                  3. Number of products: 74,258
                                                                                                                                                                  4. Timespan: Oct 1999 - Oct 2012
                                                                                                                                                                  5. Number of Attributes/Columns in data: 10


Attribute Information:
                                                                                                                                                                  1. Id
                                                                                                                                                                  2. ProductId - unique identifier for the product
                                                                                                                                                                  3. UserId - unique identifier for the user
                                                                                                                                                                  4. ProfileName
                                                                                                                                                                  5. HelpfulnessNumerator - number of users who found the review helpful (positive)
                                                                                                                                                                  6. HelpfulnessDenominator - number of users who indicated whether they found the review helpful or not( positive + negative)
                                                                                                                                                                  7. Score - rating between 1 and 5
                                                                                                                                                                  8. Time - timestamp for the review
                                                                                                                                                                  9. Summary - brief summary of the review
                                                                                                                                                                  10. Text - text of the review


Objective:
                                                                                                                                                                  * Given a review, determine whether the review is positive (Rating of 4 or 5) or negative (rating of 1 or 2).
                                                                                                                                                                  * We have to remove score column and fiell 4 or 5 column as positive and 1 or 2 as negative so, we determine from the “Text” attribute if the score is negative or positive


[Q] How to determine if a review is positive or negative?
                                                                                                                                                                  * We could use the Score/Rating. A rating of 4 or 5 could be considered a positive review. A review of 1 or 2 could be considered negative. A review of 3 is neutral and ignored. This is an approximate and proxy way of determining the polarity (positivity/negativity) of a review.


Loading the data
The dataset is available in two forms
                                                                                                                                                                  1. .csv file
                                                                                                                                                                  2. SQLite Database


                                                                                                                                                                  * In order to load the data, We have used the SQLITE dataset as it is easier to query the data and visualise the data efficiently.
                                                                                                                                                                  * Here as we only want to get the global sentiment of the recommendations (positive or negative), we will purposefully ignore all Scores equal to 3. If the score is above 3, then the recommendation will be set to "positive". Otherwise, it will be set to "negative".

#filtering only positive and negative reviews i.e.
# not taking into consideration those reviews with Score=3
# SELECT * FROM Reviews WHERE Score != 3 LIMIT 500000, will give top 500000 data points
# you can change the number to any other number based on your computing power
​
# filtered_data = pd.read_sql_query(""" SELECT * FROM Reviews WHERE Score != 3 LIMIT 500000""", con)
# for tsne assignment you can take 5k data points
​
filter_data = pd.read_sql_query("""SELECT * FROM Reviews WHERE Score != 3""", con)


# Give reviews with Score>3 a positive rating, and reviews with a score<3 a negative rating.
# 1: +ve and 0: -ve
def partition(x):
   if x < 3:
       return 0
   return 1
​
#changing reviews with score less than 3 to be positive and vice-versa
​
actualScore = filter_data['Score']
positiveNegative = actualScore.map(partition)
filter_data['Score'] = positiveNegative

Exploratory Data Analysis Data Cleaning: Deduplication
It is observed (as shown in the table below) that the reviews data had many duplicate entries.
Hence it was necessary to remove duplicates in order to get unbiased results for the analysis of the data.
Following is an example


# data cleaning
display = pd.read_sql_query("""
SELECT * FROM Reviews
WHERE Score != 3 AND UserId = "AR5J8UI46CURR"
""", con)
