                                                                                                                                                                                                                                 * After storing K smallest distances we do a majority vote and find the Yq.
                                                                                                                                                                                                                                 * Time complexity:
                                                                                                                                                                                                                                 * Here k is often small(like 5 or 10) so we ignore it and take O(1) instead.
                                                                                                                                                                                                                                 * And if d << n ( d is very very small compared to n) then we also ignore it.
                                                                                                                                                                                                                                 * So, the time complexity is O(nd)
                                                                                                                                                                                                                                 * Space: At evaluation:
                                                                                                                                                                                                                                 * Dtrain ~O(nd)
                                                                                                                                                                                                                                 * In data structure we don't require to add input data in space complexity but in machine learning the dataset is required to present in ram, so after deployment ,Dtrain is required to present in RAM.






KNN LIMITATIONS
                                                                                                                                                                                                                                 1. Due to large space and Time complexity, we will require large RAM and more time in production.
                                                                                                                                                                                                                                 2. In companese like search engines, trading, finance we useLow Latency algorithms.So most people don’t use KNN for that reason.
                                                                                                                                                                                                                                 3. We can use kd tree and LSH for improving kNN performance.






DECISION SURFACE FOR K-NN AS K CHANGES 
                                                                                                                                                                                                                                 * ‘k’ in kNN is a hyper parameter.
                                                                                                                                                                                                                                 * Curves that separate +ve points from –ve points are called decision surfaces(in n-D it is called hypersurface).
                                                                                                                                                                                                                                 *                                                                                                                                                                                                                                    * Green curve is not smooth with no errors.
                                                                                                                                                                                                                                 * Yellow curve is smooth with 2 errors.
                                                                                                                                                                                                                                 * For k = 1 :
                                                                                                                                                                                                                                    * If the query point is nearest to the one red point which is in the region of blue points then we get a red query point.
                                                                                                                                                                                                                                    * If we use many query points then we end up making the green curve which is a more jagged(rough) curve.
                                                                                                                                                                                                                                    * For k = 5: 
                                                                                                                                                                                                                                    * Yellow curve may be generated when k = 5. Because the one red point is also classified as blue point because 4 points are blue in nearest.
                                                                                                                                                                                                                                    * In KNN the smoothness of the decision surface increases as k increases.
                                                                                                                                                                                                                                    * For k = n:
                                                                                                                                                                                                                                    * n is the number of all the points.
                                                                                                                                                                                                                                    * Let n1 = 600 (all blue or positive points)
                                                                                                                                                                                                                                    * Let n2 = 400 (all red or negative points).
                                                                                                                                                                                                                                    * So if we take a query point anywhere it will take all the points because K = n. Then we get the majority class answer here we taky any query point answer will be +ve or blue point.
                                                                                                                                                                                                                                    * All query points are classified as the majority class.




OVERFITTING AND UNDERFITTING (in KNN)
                                                                                                                                                                                                                                    * Fitting:
                                                                                                                                                                                                                                    * Using the training data, the process of finding the right function f(x) is called fitting.
                                                                                                                                                                                                                                    * It comes from applied mathematics called “fitting a function to a data”.
                                                                                                                                                                                                                                    * Overfitting:
                                                                                                                                                                                                                                    * Generating extremely non smooth surfaces on training data to get extremely high accuracy on training sets.
                                                                                                                                                                                                                                    * In the previous example K = 1 is overfitting.
                                                                                                                                                                                                                                    * Underfit:
                                                                                                                                                                                                                                    * Not generating any decision surface and classifying all query points with majority class.
                                                                                                                                                                                                                                    * In the previous example K=n is underfitting.
                                                                                                                                                                                                                                    * Neither overfit nor underfit( or say well fit):
                                                                                                                                                                                                                                    * Generating smooth surfaces that are less prone or robust to noise.
                                                                                                                                                                                                                                    * In the previous example K = 5 is well fit.
                                                                                                                                                                                                                                    * In machine learning, overfit and underfit is one of the main problems we have to deal with.




NEED FOR CROSS VALIDATION
                                                                                                                                                                                                                                    * Determining k hyper parameter for kNN model:
                                                                                                                                                                                                                                    * We split the data set into train and test sets.
                                                                                                                                                                                                                                    * We train the model using a training set and compute accuracy using a test set.
                                                                                                                                                                                                                                    * For every k we determine test accuracy and select k that gives best accuracy on the test set
                                                                                                                                                                                                                                    * Ex: let we get 96% accuracy in the test dataset using K = 6.so, can we say that my accuracy is 96% in future dataset, NO.
                                                                                                                                                                                                                                    * Using a test dataset to determine the best k or best hyper parameters is not right.
                                                                                                                                                                                                                                    * We want the model to have a good generalization ability on future unseen data.
                                                                                                                                                                                                                                    * In machine learning, generalization is a definition to demonstrate how well a trained model can classify or forecast unseen data. Training a generalized machine learning model means, in general, it works for all subsets of unseen data.
                                                                                                                                                                                                                                    * Thus we split the data set into train(DTrain), cross validate(DCV) and test datasets(DTest).(roughly 60%,20%,20%).
                                                                                                                                                                                                                                    * We train the model parameters to compute nearest neighbours on DTrain, we determine best hyper parameters(or K) on DCV and we evaluate best ML models on DTest (which is unseen or never touched by the function), this will help ML models have good generalization ability.
                                                                                                                                                                                                                                    * Ex. let using DTrain and Dcv we get K = 6, now using DTest we got 93% accuracy, so we can say:
                                                                                                                                                                                                                                    * Using DTrain as training data, I find 6-NN to have 93% on future/Unseen data.
                                                                                                                                                                                                                                    * Or we can say, we have 93% of generalization accuracy.
                                                                                                                                                                                                                                    * Or we can say, we have 7% of generalization error.




K-FOLD CROSS VALIDATION
                                                                                                                                                                                                                                    * Data is split into train, cross validation and test set. While the test set should not be touched, cross validation data becomes untouched while training which will lead to loss of information. We can use k-fold cross validation to use cross validation data during training. We are trying to get the information from a cross validation set for ML model training. 
                                                                                                                                                                                                                                    1. Dataset is split randomly into DTrain and DTest  set(let say 80 %-20%)
                                                                                                                                                                                                                                    2. Train set is further divided randomly into k’ equal sized parts.(let's say k’ = 4 and the train data set is divided into equal parts D1, D2, D3, D4 each 20%).
                                                                                                                                                                                                                                    3. For each k hyper parameter in kNN, we will use ( ( k’ ) - 1)  parts of train set for training and the remaining 1 part of train set as cross validation data set, we then compute accuracy or model performance on cross validation data set, we will roll around the parts of train data set to get k’ accuracies for k = 1 (kNN hyperparameter), we will then average this accuracies for k = 1. as a result we will have an average of k’ accuracies of the train set. This is called k’-fold cross validation, we will repeat the k’ fold cross validation for all hyper parameter k value choices. 
k
	Train(part)
	CV
	accuracy
	K = 1
	D1, D2, D3
	D4
	a4
	K = 1
	D1, D2, D4
	D3
	a3
	K = 1
	D1, D3, D4
	D2
	a2
	K = 1
	D2, D3, D4
	D1
	a1
	

                                                                                                                                                                                                                                    4. We pick best k from best average k’ cross validation accuracies
                                                                                                                                                                                                                                    1. Accuracy of K=1 is average of a4 + a3 + a2 + a1 
                                                                                                                                                                                                                                    5.  And apply the best hyper parameter for measuring performance on a test set.
                                                                                                                                                                                                                                    6. Generally 10 fold cross validation is applied.
                                                                                                                                                                                                                                    7. With k’ fold cross validation time taken for finding optimal k is multiplied by k’ times.
                                                                                                                                                                                                                                    8. But finding optimal k is a one time effort.




 VISUALISING TRAIN, VALIDATION AND TEST DATASETS
                                                                                                                                                                                                                                    * When we split data in Dtrain , Dtest, Dcv randomly then the dtest , not overlap with dcv or Dtrain because the data is from dn .
                                                                                                                                                                                                                                    * If we find maximum positive or negative point form Dtrain in particular region the there is high probability that we find positive point from Dtest and Dcv in that particular region.
                                                                                                                                                                                                                                    * But there are always outliers or noise which we can find in data.


HOW TO DETERMINE OVERFITTING AND UNDERFITTING?


                                                                                                                                                                                                                                    * We are finding best k that is neither underfitting nor overfitting; 
                                                                                                                                                                                                                                    * Accuracy: # correctly classified points/ total # of points 
                                                                                                                                                                                                                                    * Error: 1 – accuracy
                                                                                                                                                                                                                                    * Training error:
                                                                                                                                                                                                                                    * When we use DTrain for both training and cross validation/accuracy/error.
                                                                                                                                                                                                                                    * Let's say K=2 so we take a point from DTrain xi and compute 2-NN and compute the class label and match with the actual class label and if it is true then accurate else error.
                                                                                                                                                                                                                                    * cross validation error:
                                                                                                                                                                                                                                    * When we use DTrain for training and DCV for error/accuracy.
                                                                                                                                                                                                                                    * Test error:
                                                                                                                                                                                                                                    * It is unseen by the function; we only use it to report how a good function is.
                                                                                                                                                                                                                                    * Plot a curve on error vs k hyperparameter.
                                                                                                                                                                                                                                    *                                                                                                                                                                                                                                       * If train error is high and validation error is high then we are underfitting.
                                                                                                                                                                                                                                    * If train error is low and validation error is high then we are overfitting.
                                                                                                                                                                                                                                    * At optimal k we will have closer train error and validation error.(in above graph k = 5 is optimal solution)




 TIME BASED SPLITTING 
                                                                                                                                                                                                                                       * Data was split randomly so far, For Amazon fine food reviews time based splitting is better as we also have a timestamp feature in the dataset.
                                                                                                                                                                                                                                       * We will sort the data in the ascending order of timestamp.(oldest 60% for train next 20% for cross validation and next 20% for test).
                                                                                                                                                                                                                                       *  If timestamps are available we need to check which of the random split or time based split is better.
                                                                                                                                                                                                                                       * In random splitting: 
                                                                                                                                                                                                                                       * we will get reviews that were written before will occur in the test set and the reviews that were written after will occur in the train set.
                                                                                                                                                                                                                                       * In time based splitting:
                                                                                                                                                                                                                                       * we will get reviews in train, cross validation and test set based on timestamps, the reviews that were written first occur in train set, then in cross validation and then in test set.
                                                                                                                                                                                                                                       * The argument here is we should avoid predicting past data based on models trained on future datasets. Reviews or products change over time. new products get added or some products get terminated. As time passes we require retraining the model with new data.(means we always use the test dataset as the newest and followed by cross validation and oldest train dataset).
                                                                                                                                                                                                                                       * Whenever time is available and if things behave or data changes over time then doing time based splitting is preferable.






K-NN FOR REGRESSION
                                                                                                                                                                                                                                       *  For Classification: 
                                                                                                                                                                                                                                       * Dn = {(xi, yi) | xi ε Rd , yi ε {0, 1}} (class label)
                                                                                                                                                                                                                                       * We do the majority vote.
                                                                                                                                                                                                                                       * For Regression:
                                                                                                                                                                                                                                       *  Dn = {(xi, yi) | xi ε Rd , yi ε R} (a real number)
                                                                                                                                                                                                                                       * we will do mean or median of all k neighbours
                                                                                                                                                                                                                                       *                                                                                                                                                                                                                                        *                                                                                                                                                                                                                                           * For some algorithms we can easily extend classification problems to regression problems.




WEIGHTED K-NN
                                                                                                                                                                                                                                          *                                                                                                                                                                                                                                             * Let assume in the above diagram, there are 5 neighbours 2 -ve and 3 +ve
                                                                                                                                                                                                                                          * Distance of each are:
                                                                                                                                                                                                                                             * 0.1
                                                                                                                                                                                                                                             * 0.2
                                                                                                                                                                                                                                             * 1.0
                                                                                                                                                                                                                                             * 2.0
                                                                                                                                                                                                                                             * 4.0
                                                                                                                                                                                                                                             * So by majority vote the query point is positive but by weighted knn we can use distance as a weight in choosing the class label.
                                                                                                                                                                                                                                             * There are many ways we can use weighted knn but simplest of all are inverse function.(1/distance)
                                                                                                                                                                                                                                             * So from above :
                                                                                                                                                                                                                                             *                                                                                                                                                                                                                                              *                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                 * Closer points will have high weights.
                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                * So, by weighted Knn we say that the query point is negative.




VORONOI DIAGRAM (link)
                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                *                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                   * This divides the whole data space into regions based on nearest neighbour where k =  1.
                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                * If a point falls into any of the cells then the nearest point is the black point in that region.
                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                * You can make a voronoi diagram by taking k = 1.




 BINARY SEARCH TREE kNN:
                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                   * Time complexity: O(n) if d is small and k is small.
                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                   * Space complexity: O(n) 
                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                   * We can reduce time complexity to O(log n) using kd tree.
                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                   * Binary search tree: Given a sorted array, we can find presence of a number in the array in O(log n) time.
                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                   * Construct a binary search tree, find element in array through comparisons.
                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                   *  Depth of BST is O(log n)




HOW TO BUILD A KD-TREE BST:
                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                   * Given a list of sorted numbers we can build a tree that divides the list in two at every stage 
                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                   * Kd – Tree:
                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                   * Pick the first axis and project all data points onto the axis.
                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                   * pick the middle point; draw a plane through the middle point this divides the space into two equal halves;
                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                   * Change the axis to y and repeat the steps.
                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                   * Change to x axis again and repeat steps.
                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                   * The data space is broken using axis parallel lines(2D) or hyper planes/cuboids(3D) or into hyper planes/cuboids(nd).
                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                   * We go through each axis alternate one after another till leaf node.
                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                   *   



FIND NEAREST NEIGHBOURS USING KD-TREE
  

                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                      *  xq <= x1, yq >= y1, xq >= x5  c is one of the nearest points.
                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                      * Draw a hyper sphere with center xq and radius Dist(c,q); 
                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                      * If there is another point is inside the hypersphere; this can also be checked as the hyper sphere intersects with y = y1 line; 
                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                      * We track back to y <= y1 condition in the tree and search for another nearest data point; 
                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                      * now point e can also be a nearest neighbor; 
                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                      * Dist(q, e) < Dist(c,e): thus c is discarded as 1 nearest neighbor and take e as nearest neighbor; 
                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                      * we repeat the steps done with c now with e; we can have a result that point e is the nearest neighbor to query point q; 
                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                      * Best case Time complexity:
                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                      * Best case: O(log n)
                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                      * worst case : O(n).
                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                      * For k Nearest Neighbors Time complexities: 
                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                      * Best case: O(k log n) 
                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                      * Worst case: O(kn) 




LIMITATIONS OF KD TREE 
                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                      * As dimensionality increases the number of back tracks in kd tree worsens time complexity;
                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                      * When d is not small like{2,3,4,5} , d is like {10,20,1000} then so for finding 1-NN:
                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                      * Time complex: o(log n)( for small d)
                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                      * TIme complex: o(2d log(n)) ( for big d)
                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                      * o(2d log(n)) is worse then o(n) bruteforce method.
                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                      * kd tree nearest neighbor updates is exponentially proportional to dimensionality (2d) 
                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                      * O(log n) is valid for uniform distribution and as distribution moves towards real world clusters, time complexity moves towards O(n).
                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                      * Kd tree usually use in computer graphics which has 2d or 3d data.




 EXTENSIONS 
                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                      * Go through Wikipedia article




HASHING VS LSH 
                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                      * Locality sensitive hashing to find nearest neighbors when d is large.
                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                      * Given an unordered array we apply a hash function, when we need to find an element in the array we can use the hash table, we make the array element, key of the hash table and the value is indices of the array so when we search the element we get the indices in a constant time.
                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                      * Locality sensitive hashing:
                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                      * It computes a hash function such that nearest data points(local or similar) pairs are stored in the same bucket.
                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                      * for a new query point relevant bucket is searched in the hash table.
                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                      * And k nearest neighbors are searched through data points in this bucket.
                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                      * This will reduce the need for searching throughout the data space.
                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                      *   



LSH FOR COSINE SIMILARITY 
                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                         * cos_sim(x1, x2) = cos θ 
                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                         * As θ increases between the points the cosine decreases.
                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                         * Similarity decreases when angular distance increases.
                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                         * LSH is a randomized algorithm.
                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                         * Randomized algorithm says:
                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                         * It will not always give you the correct answer.
                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                         * But it will give the right answer with high probability.
                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                         * If two points are close in terms of angular distance, then the points are similar.
                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                         * These points should go to the same bucket in the hash table.
                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                         *                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                            * f1 and f2: feature 1,2(2d space)
                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                         * x1,x2 and x3 are points
                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                         * We break(angularly) feature space using random hyperplanes(Π1,Π2,...Πm).
                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                         *  for every plane we will have a unit normal vector ‘w1, w2,...wn’ 
                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                         * Hyperplanes break a region just like a pizza slice.
                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                         * For plane (Π1): Say we have x1 above and x2 below the hyper planes.
                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                            * we will have: w1T . x1 >=0  and w1T . x2 <=0 
                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                            * Random hyperplanes are wT. x = 0 where w is a d-dimensional random vector.
                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                            * Random hyper planes are generated by generating a random W vector.
                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                            * Each value in the W vector is randomly generated from Normal distribution N(0,1)(0 mean and 1 variance).
                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                            * For generating random hyperplane in python :
                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                            *  numpy.random.normal(0,1,d) where d is dimension


How we create a hash function
                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                            * Let we have m number of hyperlanes then we have m-dimensional vector for every slice of the feature space.
                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                            * We give each slice a m-dimensional vector where sign of the  wT.xq makes the vector example
                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                            * We have three hyperplanes (Π1,Π2,Π3)
                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                            * We take any point in a slice, let say we take x1.
                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                            * X1 is above all three plane  w1T.x1 ->+ve, w2T.x1 ->+ve and w3T.x1 ->+ve
                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                            * H(x1) = [+1,+1,+1], similarly
                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                            * H(x2) = [-1,+1,+1]
                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                            * H(x3) = [+1, -1, -1]
                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                            * Now with the hash function we create a hash table where the key is the hash function value we created and all the points are stored in a corresponding value bucket. 
                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                            * Space complexity O(nd)
                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                            * n is the number of points and every point belongs to any of one slice so we need to store each point once.
                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                            * Unlike the k-d tree in LSH d could be large so, we cannot ignore d.
                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                            * Time to construct the hash table O(mdn) :
                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                            * m hyper planes
                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                            * d dimensionality
                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                            * n data points Space
                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                            * Every point is multiplied with m hyperplane(wT.xn) which has d dimension of approx ~ O(mdn)
                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                            * Now when a new query point comes xq we compute hash function of that and and search in the hash table which gives all set of points near that from which we can compute K-NN (hash_table.get(H(xq)) → {x1,x2,..xn} in that region or slice.
                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                            * We have to compute xq to every m number of hyperplanes which is O(md) where d is dimensionality of the query point.
                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                            * After that the query point is compared with all the points in the bucket let there is n’ number of points in the bucket,then the total complexity for knn is O(md + n’d).
                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                            * If n is small or approx the value of m (n ~ m) then we can write O(md).
                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                            * So people set m roughly to log(n) so the overall complexity become O(d * log(n))
                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                            * LSH for cosine similarity can miss nearest neighbors when the nearest neighbor falls on the opposite side to any hyperplane.
                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                            * So for not missing the nearest neighbors we have to make multiple set of hash table example we create a hash table x1,x2,x3….xl where L is number of hash table then we compute the query point and get points from each hash table, 
                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                            * Now we take a union of points from each hash table and make a big set and then take the nearest neighbor from that.
                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                            * So the final complexity to query a given point in the L number of the hash table is O(mdL).
                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                            * If number of hyperplanes increase then the number of slices also increases and we get very few number of points in a region and if number of hyperplanes decrease then the number of the points in a particular region is very large so we have to compute with lot of points so we have to choose number of hyperplane.
                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                            * General rule of thumb is we take m = O(log(n)).




LSH FOR EUCLIDEAN DISTANCE
                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                            *                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                               * Similar/closer points should get in the same bucket.
                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                            * Let there be m number of hyperplanes we project each point perpendicular to each hyperplane.
                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                            * X21 projection of point x2 in Π1 hyperplane.
                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                            * Every point is projected on each plane of the data space.
                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                            *                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                               * Each plane is divided into units.
                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                            * For above there is 8 unit -3,-2,....4
                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                            * How we create hash function:
                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                               * H(x11) = [2,.....] (size of vector is m which is number of hyperplane)
                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                               * H(x31) = [-3,....]
                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                               * In H(x11) we put every hyperplane region number in the [2,...] vector.
                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                               * And we get the vector for every point which will become key for our hash table.
                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                               * Unlike cosine LSH which is +1 or -1,  euclidian LSH has any number in it.
                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                               * Now we do it with L number of hash table which will become key for each hash table and do as above.
                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                               *                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                  * Now x2 and x1 if far away but falls in same region in Π1,
                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                               * But in another hyperplane(vertical) the two are far away so there is a high chance that the points which are further away fall in different regions but there is some plane where both fall overlapping.
                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                               * LSH if not perfect it is a probabilistic/randomized algorithm that gives you probabilistic guarantee .
                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                               * It says i will find knn with some probability
                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                               * LSH is used extensively in computer vision.




PROBABILISTIC CLASS LABEL
                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                  * Let we get 7NN for  a point xq where 4 points are  +ve and 3 are –ve.
                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                  * say another query data point yq has 7 +ve and 0 –ve neighbors.
                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                  * Then both the cases give prediction as +ve based on majority vote.
                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                  * but both data points do not have the same number of +ve number of data points, query data point xq is less +ve than query data point yq.
                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                  * thus giving a probabilistic quantification of the prediction will give us more confidence.
                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                  * xq has 4/7 +ve and 3/7 –ve.
                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                  * yq has 7/7 +ve and 0/7 –ve.
                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                  * This gives a certain statistic of predictions. 




CODE SAMPLE: DECISION BOUNDARY
                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                  *  sklearn.neighbors.KNeighbirsClassifier()
                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                  *  As k increases the decision boundary smoothens;
                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                  * Below is a code to visualize 2-D KNN using meshgrid
import numpy as np
import matplotlib.pyplot as plt
from sklearn import datasets, neighbors
from matplotlib.colors import ListedColormap
from sklearn.neighbors import KNeighborsClassifier
​
def knn_comparision(data, n_neighbors = 15):
   X = data[:, :2]
   y = data[:,2]
  
  
#grid cell size
   h = .02
  
#for surface
   cmap_light = ListedColormap(['#FFAAAA',  '#AAAAFF'])
# for points
   cmap_bold = ListedColormap(['#FF0000', '#0000FF'])
  
   clf = KNeighborsClassifier(n_neighbors)
   clf.fit(X,y)
  #x and y minimum and maximum for taking upper and lower limit in grid
   x_min, x_max = X[:, 0].min() - 1, X[:, 0].max() + 1
   y_min, y_max = X[:, 1].min() - 1, X[:, 1].max() + 1
  
   # we create a mesh grid (x_min,y_min) to (x_max y_max) with 0.02 grid spaces
   xx, yy = np.meshgrid(np.arange(x_min, x_max, h), np.arange(y_min, y_max, h))
  
   # we predict the value (either 0 or 1) of each element in the grid
   Z = clf.predict(np.c_[xx.ravel(), yy.ravel()])
  
  
   # convert the out back to the xx shape (we need it to plot the decision boundary)
   Z = Z.reshape(xx.shape)
  
  
   # pcolormesh will plot the (xx,yy) grid with colors according to the values of Z
   # it looks like decision boundary
   plt.figure()
